Every changed line traces to "CPV import = the last C-3 capability". Cleared to commit.**

- **2026-06-10 · App-shell a11y debt close — Layout mobile nav-drawer focus-trap (the lone Slice-8 keyboard-nav carve-out) + axe open-overlay scans (working tree, uncommitted; `Layout.tsx` + `e2e/a11y.spec.ts` + NEW `e2e/layout.spec.ts`). VERDICT: PASS (no must-fix, no FLAG).** Read the full diff + `Layout.tsx` + `useFocusTrap.ts` end-to-end; the gating risk was a trap wrongly arming at desktop and imprisoning every keyboard user in the sidebar on every page.
  - **Trap-active condition `open && !wide` — CORRECT, and `wide` is genuinely REACTIVE.** `useState(isWide)` seeds `wide` (Layout.tsx:98); the effect (99-104) subscribes `mq.addEventListener('change', onChange)` on `(min-width:1024px)` and `removeEventListener` in cleanup — symmetric, deps `[]` so one stable subscription for the component life. A mobile→desktop resize while the drawer is open flips `wide=true` → `drawerTrapActive=open && !wide` recomputes false on the next render → the `useFocusTrap` `[active]` effect tears down (removes keydown, runs restore-focus). Desktop carve-out holds: at `lg+` the trap can never be active regardless of `open`. The `lg:static` in-flow nav at `lg+` is therefore never trapped.
  - **Hook does NOT re-run on the fresh `() => setOpen(false)` closure each render — confirmed by reading the hook.** `useFocusTrap` deps are `[active]` only (useFocusTrap.ts:91); `onEscape` is stored to `onEscapeRef.current` on every render (34-35) and read late inside `onKeyDown` (60). So a new handler identity per render does NOT re-grab focus or rebind. Same latest-ref contract the 13 existing dialog/menu consumers rely on (DataGrid menus, MasterDataCrud, all admin dialogs). New `<aside>` consumer matches that pattern exactly.
  - **No double-source-of-truth between `open` and `wide`.** They seed from the same `isWide()` but model orthogonal concerns: `open` = drawer visibility (user toggles via hamburger; persists across breakpoints), `wide` = live breakpoint. They are never required to agree. `closeOnMobileNav` correctly switched from imperative `isWide()` (105-107) to the reactive `wide` state — strictly better: it reads the same render-consistent value the trap condition uses, so close-on-nav and trap-arming can't disagree mid-render. `aria-expanded={open}` / `aria-label` on the hamburger still key off `open` — correct.
  - **`<HTMLElement>` ref on `<aside>` — valid (`HTMLElement` is the base of every element type; `aside` has no dedicated interface). When closed, `className="hidden"` (display:none) but `open===false` ⇒ `drawerTrapActive===false` ⇒ the hook effect early-returns at `if (!active)` (useFocusTrap.ts:38), so the ref-on-a-hidden-node is inert. No dead code, no orphan: the `useEffect`/`useState` import additions, `wide`, the effect, `drawerTrapActive`, `drawerRef` are all consumed.** `focusables()` filters `offsetParent !== null` so a `display:none` subtree would yield zero focusables anyway — defence in depth.
  - **Tests — sound.** `layout.spec.ts` asserts the FULL contract at 390px: focus moves to first focusable (Cases — Dashboard/Pipeline render as `aria-disabled` divs with no `href`, correctly skipped by `FOCUSABLE_SELECTOR`'s `a[href]`), Escape closes + restores focus to the hamburger. `a11y.spec.ts` `expectNoGatedViolations` extraction is a pure refactor (byte-equivalent axe call) + 2 OPEN-overlay scans (modal dialog, mobile drawer) — closes the "axe only saw closed pages" gap. Verification accepted (`pnpm verify` EXIT=0, api 358/358 unaffected; Playwright a11y+datagrid+layout all green; live preview confirmed). **No must-fix. Every changed line traces to the two carried ledger items. Cleared to commit.**

### 2026-06-15 — B-7.1 background-job engine (ADR-0030; `platform/jobs/{index,repository}.ts` + `modules/jobs/{service,controller,routes}.ts` + `sdk/jobs.ts` + `0050_jobs.sql` + app.ts/client.ts diffs; working tree, uncommitted) — VERDICT: PASS (no BLOCK; 2 SHOULD-FIX, neither gating)
  - **Seam-template parity — faithful to `platform/realtime`.** Same config-gated factory shape: `enqueue` reads `loadEnv().REDIS_QUEUE_URL` and degrades to in-process when unset, exactly as realtime degrades to its in-memory adapter when `REDIS_CACHE_URL` is unset. The `setJobNotifier`/`notifier:JobNotifier|null` injectable mirrors realtime's `setRealtime`/`override` and storage/geocode's `setStorage`/`setGeocoder`. `getRealtime()` reused for emits (no second socket path). Both queue paths funnel through ONE `runJob` (index.ts:71) → the progress/done/notify contract is identical regardless of tier. Sound extension seam.
  - **CORRECTNESS — engine: PASS.** (1) **in-flight tracking is leak-free.** `runJob` is wrapped in `.catch(log)` (index.ts:130-132) so the promise added to `inFlight` (133) can NEVER reject; `void run.finally(() => inFlight.delete(run))` (134) deletes by the SAME reference (the caught promise, not the raw `runJob` promise) → set entry always removed, success or crash. `awaitAllJobs` snapshots `[...inFlight]` so a job that finishes mid-await is fine; jobs *enqueued after* the snapshot are intentionally not awaited (correct for a test-sync helper). No unbounded growth. (2) **`setRunning WHERE status='PENDING'` race — benign.** The guarded UPDATE only matters if the same job is dispatched twice; the in-process path dispatches each `job.id` exactly once (single `enqueue`), and the later `setProgress`/`setSucceeded`/`setFailed` UPDATEs are unguarded `WHERE id=$1` — acceptable because a single runner owns the row end-to-end (no concurrent writer until the BullMQ worker lands, and BullMQ gives once-only delivery). The `WHERE status='PENDING'` guard is the right forward-defense for the worker slice (a redelivered job won't re-stamp `started_at`). (3) **progress clamp correct** — `clampPct = max(0,min(100,round(n)))` (index.ts:55) handles NaN→`Math.round(NaN)=NaN`… *see SHOULD-FIX #1*. (4) **failed-path code capture sound** — `e instanceof AppError ? e.code : e instanceof Error ? e.message : 'JOB_FAILED'` (index.ts:102): structured AppError → stable `.code`, plain Error → message, non-Error throw → literal fallback; matches the migration's `error text -- the AppError code/message (no stack)` comment, no stack leak. (5) **no missed await** — every repo write is awaited inside `runJob`; `enqueue` awaits `insert` before dispatch (so the returned `JobView` is the real PENDING row) then deliberately does NOT await `runJob` (fire-after-response is the whole point) — and that floating run IS voided+caught (index.ts:130-134). The `progress` callback awaits `setProgress` before emitting. No floating promise escapes uncaught in the platform layer.
  - **LAYERING / BOUNDARIES — PASS.** `grep 'modules/' platform/jobs/*.ts` = 0: platform/jobs imports only `@crm2/config`, `@crm2/logger`, `@crm2/sdk` (types), `../errors`, `../realtime`, `./repository` — no module dependency. The completion notifier is INJECTED from app.ts (`setJobNotifier`) so `notificationService` (a module) is never imported by platform — same inversion as `setRealtime`. Module→platform direction is correct & precedented: `modules/jobs/service.ts` imports `platform/jobs/repository` exactly as `modules/notifications/service` imports its platform repo. Raw SQL lives ONLY in `platform/jobs/repository.ts` (precedent cited in-file: `platform/import/importLog.repository.ts` — confirmed, that file is platform-resident raw SQL too). Controller imports only the service + AppError — no controller→repo leak. dependency-cruiser's 0-errors is consistent with what I read.
  - **PATTERN REUSE — PASS, zero reinvention.** `service.list` uses `resolvePage(rawQuery, JOB_PAGE_SPEC)` + `Promise.all([listOwned, countOwned])` + `buildPage` — byte-identical structure to `notifications/service.list` (the cited mirror). `JOB_PAGE_SPEC.sortMap={createdAt:'created_at'}` whitelists the only sortable col; `listOwned` ORDER BY uses `${p.sortColumn}` (whitelisted) — injection-safe. Controller reuses the `requireUserId` pattern + the `UUID_RE` shape-guard (identical regex + rationale comment as the notifications/other uuid-param controllers) so a bad `:id` is a clean 404 not a pg-22P02 500. `AppError.notFound()`/`unauthenticated()` factories reused. `query<T>` reused. `countOwned` uses `count(*)::text`→`Number(...)` (notifications-count idiom). **TS-strict clean:** no `any`, no non-null-assertion, no `console.*`, no suppressions in any source file (the only `!`-style is none; `row` null-guarded via `if (!row) throw`). SDK `jobs` block reuses `pageQueryToParams` + `Paginated<JobView>` + the `req<T>` helper exactly like `notifications.list`.
  - **API SHAPE — PASS, additive-only.** `GET /api/v2/jobs` → `Paginated<JobView>`, `GET /api/v2/jobs/:id` → `JobView`; both NEW routes under `/api/v2`, nothing existing altered (app.ts diff is a 1-line route mount + the notifier injection block). SDK matches server 1:1 (`list(q)→Paginated<JobView>`, `get(id)→JobView`); `index.ts` re-exports `./jobs.js`. `JobView` excludes `payload` (READ_COLS omits it; repo comment + migration confirm payload is server-internal) — no input leak to clients. SDK enums (`JOB_TYPES`/`JOB_STATUSES`) match the migration CHECKs; `NOTIFICATION_TYPES`/`NOTIFICATION_ACTION_TYPES` widened to `JOB_COMPLETED`/`JOB_FAILED`/`DOWNLOAD` in lockstep with `0050`'s CHECK-rewrite (verified both sides). `NotifyInput` shape (userId/type/title/payload?/actionType?) exactly satisfies the notifier call sites.
  - **B-13/B-14 extension contract — SOUND, no rewrite risk.** `JobContext{jobId,userId,payload:unknown,progress(pct,stage?)}` + `JobProcessor=(ctx)=>Promise<Record<string,unknown>>` is the right plug-point: export (B-13) registers an EXPORT processor that returns `{storageKey,filename,rowCount}` (matches the `JobResultUrl`/`result` shape already declared in sdk/jobs.ts + the migration's `result` comment); import (B-14) registers an IMPORT processor. `registerJobProcessor`/`hasJobProcessor` + the `DONE_TITLE`/`FAIL_TITLE` per-`JobType` records + `actionType: type==='EXPORT'?'DOWNLOAD':'NAVIGATE'` already branch both types. `payload:unknown` forces each processor to validate its own input (correct — the engine is payload-agnostic). No design smell that forces a next-slice rewrite; the only swap-in is dispatch (in-process → BullMQ), and `runJob` is already the shared sink for both.
  - **SHOULD-FIX (non-gating):** (1) `clampPct(NaN)` → `Math.max(0, Math.min(100, NaN))` = `NaN`, written to a `progress int CHECK (progress BETWEEN 0 AND 100)` column → the `setProgress` UPDATE would throw (CHECK violation / invalid-int) and surface as a job FAILURE. A processor passing `NaN`/`Infinity` is a processor bug, but a `Number.isFinite(n) ? ... : 0` guard in `clampPct` would harden the engine boundary against its own consumers (cheap, B-13/B-14 will be the first real callers). (2) the injected notifier `(n) => { void notificationService.notify(n); }` (app.ts) swallows a notify REJECTION (DB insert failure) as an unhandled void — the notifier type is `=> void` so it can't be awaited inside `runJob`, and a failed notification would silently drop with no log. Mirror the realtime "best-effort" comment but add a `.catch(logger.warn)` so a dropped bell is at least observable. Neither blocks the slice; both are boundary-hardening for the worker/export slices.
  - **NOTE (not a finding):** `enqueue` logs "REDIS_QUEUE_URL set but BullMQ worker not yet wired — running in-process" then falls through to the in-process path even when the queue URL IS set. Intentional & ADR-0030-documented (the contract is exercised until the worker role lands) — but once B-7.2 wires BullMQ, that fall-through MUST become an early `return job` after enqueueing to Valkey, or a queue-configured prod would double-run (in-process AND worker). Carry as a worker-slice gate. **Cleared. No must-fix.**

### 2026-06-15 — B-13 EXPORT-as-job slice (ADR-0030 / ADR-0021; `platform/export/job.ts` + `http/registerJobs.ts` NEW; `modules/jobs/{service,controller,routes}.ts`, `modules/locations/{service,controller}.ts`, `platform/http.ts`, `http/app.ts`, `sdk/{client,client.test}.ts`, `jobs.api.test.ts` diffs; working tree, uncommitted, on bf8fdc7) — VERDICT: FLAG (no BLOCK; 1 must-fix F1, 1 SHOULD-FIX)
  - **(1) ExportBuild closure registry + variance — SOUND.** `Map<string, ExportBuild>` with `registerExportBuilder` (last-write-wins, idempotent for per-test `createApp`, matches `registerJobProcessor`/`setJobNotifier`). The generic `buildExportFile<T>(rows:T[], columns:ExportColumn<T>[], cols, base, format)` is the variance escape hatch: the `ExportBuild` signature is **non-generic** (`query, actorId, cols, format) => Promise<{body,filename,rowCount}>` — the `T` is fully closed INSIDE each module's registered closure (`registerJobs.ts:15-18`: `locationService.exportAllForJob(query).then(({rows,columns}) => buildExportFile(rows, columns, cols, 'locations', format))`), where `rows` and `columns` are the SAME `T=Location` from one call, so `ExportColumn<Location>[]` meets `T[]` with no variance hole. The engine's `builders` map never sees `T` — it only ever holds `(…)=>Promise<{body,filename,rowCount}>`, a concrete type. This correctly sidesteps the `ExportColumn<T>` invariance problem that a `Map<string, {rows, columns:ExportColumn<T>}>` would have hit (you cannot store heterogeneous `ExportColumn<T>` in one container without `unknown`+cast). Clean extension point: a new resource = one `registerExportBuilder` line + one `exportAllForJob` method, zero engine change.
  - **(2) `exportOrEnqueue` headers-sent race — PROVEN SAFE.** Traced `svc.exportData` (locations/service.ts:131-154): it runs `repo.list` then `if (ex.mode==='all') assertExportable(totalCount)` (line 153) and only THEN `return {rows,columns}`. `assertExportable` throws `EXPORT_TOO_LARGE` (413) BEFORE the return. In `exportOrEnqueue` (job.ts:99-107) the throw happens inside `await opts.run(ex)` — `writeExport` (the only thing that touches `res`) is on the NEXT line and is never reached. `writeExport` itself (export/index.ts) builds the body fully in memory and calls `res.setHeader`/`res.send` as its final two statements — so even if it WERE entered, no header is emitted until after a successful build. Net: at the `catch` (job.ts:108) `res` is pristine → `res.status(202).json(job)` cannot collide with an already-sent stream. The narrow guard (`e.code==='EXPORT_TOO_LARGE' && builders.has(resource)`) re-throws everything else to `next(e)` (honest 413 for unregistered resources — incremental rollout). No double-send, no partial write.
  - **(3) LAYERING — `registerJobs` in `http/` is CLEAN; `platform/export/job.ts` importing platform/jobs + platform/storage is ALLOWED.** `registerJobs.ts` lives at the boot/http layer and is the ONLY thing that imports a feature module (`modules/locations/service`) into the job-processor wiring — mirroring how `app.ts` injects `notificationService` via `setJobNotifier`. The engine (`platform/export/job.ts`) imports only `platform/{errors,http,jobs,storage,export}` — all platform-internal, sibling-platform deps (export→jobs→storage is intra-platform, the same direction `platform/jobs/index` already imports `platform/realtime`). grep-confirm: `platform/export/job.ts` has 0 `modules/` imports. So the job ENGINE stays module-free; module knowledge enters only at the http boot seam. Correct inversion, precedented.
  - **(4) WORKER (B-7.2) payload self-sufficiency — VERIFIED for locations; CARRY for actor-scoped resources.** `ExportJobPayload{resource, query, format, cols, actorId}` (job.ts:59-65) is 100% JSON-serializable — no closure, no `req`, no `res` captured. `exportJobProcessor` (job.ts:68-78) reconstructs everything from `ctx.payload` + the boot-registered `builders.get(resource)` (the worker re-runs `registerJobs()` at its own boot, so the closure is re-created in-process, NOT serialized — correct). `locations.exportAllForJob(query)` takes ONLY `rawQuery` and re-derives every filter/sort from it (service.ts:162-178) — no actor scope needed (global catalog), so the worker reproduces the exact same query a different process. **CARRY (already flagged in the slice's own comment):** tasks/cases ARE actor-scoped — when they adopt this, `exportAllForJob` MUST re-resolve scope from `actorId` (it's in the payload, good) via `userScope`/`dataScope`, NOT trust a `query` that the original request had already scoped. The payload carries `actorId` precisely for this; the contract is ready, the discipline is on the future adopter. No rewrite risk to the engine.
  - **(5) TS-strict / no-any / no-suppressions — PASS.** grep across all 6 slice source files: 0 `any`/`as any`/`@ts-ignore`/`@ts-expect-error`/`eslint-disable`/`console.*`. Two `as` casts, both narrowings of `unknown` at a deserialization boundary, both re-guarded: `ctx.payload as ExportJobPayload` (job.ts:69, then `if (!build) throw NO_EXPORT_BUILDER`), `job.result as {storageKey?,filename?}` (jobs/service.ts, then `if (!result.storageKey) throw JOB_NO_ARTIFACT`). `buildExportFile<T>`/`exportOrEnqueue<T>` generics thread cleanly; `ExportBuild` is a precise function type; `HTTP_STATUS.ACCEPTED:202` added to the const map (used at job.ts:111). SDK `resultUrl` typed `req<JobResultUrl>`.
  - **F1 · MUST-FIX (data-correctness, also CEO-flagged) · `modules/locations/service.ts:166-177` (`exportAllForJob`)** — destructures `const { items } = await repo.list({…, limit: exportJobRowCap()=100_000})` and **drops the `totalCount`** the same query returns (`repository.ts:70`). 157k catalog → stores 100k, `rowCount:100_000`, job SUCCEEDS, 57k rows silently gone — no `capped` flag, no log. Engineering fix: `const { items, totalCount } = await repo.list(...)`; if `totalCount > items.length`, the processor result must carry `capped:true, totalCount` AND `logger.warn('export capped', {resource, totalCount, cap})` (or fail the job with an `AppError`). The data is already in hand — this is a one-destructure + one-branch change. Proper long fix is the streaming builder the file header (job.ts:18) already promises, which lifts the cap; until then, do not emit a silent partial. (The live "157k→13MB CSV" verification was almost certainly a truncated ~100k file.)
  - **SHOULD-FIX (non-gating, carries from B-7.1) · `http/app.ts` injected notifier `void notificationService.notify(n)` has no `.catch`** — unchanged by this slice but now actually exercised end-to-end (real EXPORT jobs fire JOB_COMPLETED/DOWNLOAD). Still the only unhandled-rejection path; wrap with `.catch(logger.warn)`. Already on both ledgers (B-7.1 F1 / SHOULD-FIX #2); reiterating because B-13 makes it a live path.
  - **NOTE (not a finding):** `MAX_EXPORT_ROWS=100_000` is a hard-coded platform const (job.ts:19) while its sibling `EXPORT_JOB_THRESHOLD` is env-backed (`loadEnv`). Acceptable as an engine guard rail, but consider env-tuning it alongside the threshold when the streaming builder lands. **Cleared after F1.**


### 2026-06-15 — B-7 FE background-jobs slice (ADR-0030; NEW `components/JobsTray.tsx` + `features/jobs/{api,useJobs}.ts`; `sdk/export.ts` `ExportOutcome`, `lib/sdk.ts` `apiExport`, `ui/data-grid/DataGrid.tsx`, `NotificationBell.tsx`, `Layout.tsx`, 13 pages + MasterDataCrud `apiBlob→apiExport`; working tree, uncommitted) — VERDICT: PASS (no BLOCK, no must-fix; 1 FLAG-minor, 1 INFO)

Read every new file + the full `git diff` end-to-end. Verified independently: `pnpm --filter @crm2/web typecheck` EXIT 0; prettier `--check` on all slice files clean; `pnpm boundaries` 0 errors (14 pre-existing orphan warnings, all e2e/config, unrelated); grep across slice = 0 `any`/`as any`/`@ts-ignore`/`@ts-expect-error`/`eslint-disable`.

- **(1) `ExportOutcome` union + `apiExport` 202-detection — CORRECT and robust.** `ExportOutcome = {kind:'file';blob;filename} | {kind:'job';job:JobView}` (export.ts:45), discriminated, exhaustively handled in DataGrid `runExport` (`out.kind==='job'` → toast+invalidate+return; else blob-download). `apiExport` (sdk.ts) treats ONLY 202 as a job (`res.json()→JobView`); ANY other 2xx is a file (`res.blob()` + Content-Disposition filename). Probed both ways: (a) **could a 202 carry a file?** No — the BE answers 202 exclusively from `exportOrEnqueue`'s catch with `res.status(202).json(job)` (no body stream); a synchronous file is always 200 via `writeExport`. (b) **could a 200 carry JSON that misparses as a blob?** A 200 is unconditionally `res.blob()` — it is NEVER `.json()`'d, so there is no JSON-parse path to misfire on a 200; a hypothetical JSON-200 would become a blob with a default "export" filename (degraded, not a crash). The contract is BE-enforced (202⇔job, else⇔file) and the FE mirror is the strict, safe reading. Error path: `!res.ok` → `JSON.parse(text)` → `ApiError(status, json?.error, json)` — same shape as `apiBlob`, preserves the single-flight 401-refresh (recursion `apiExport(path,true)` after `refreshOnce`). Sound.
- **(2) `useRealtimeJobs` cache-patch — race-safe, leak-free.** `job:progress` reads `qc.getQueryData(JOBS_KEY)` fresh on each fire (no stale closure — `qc` is the only dep and is stable from `useQueryClient`); if the row exists it `setQueryData` patches in place (smooth Hexagon %, no refetch flicker); if ABSENT it `invalidateQueries` (a brand-new job appears immediately). `job:done` always invalidates (the event carries no result body — refetch pulls final status + artifact pointer; correct, matches the BE which emits done without the result). **Race analysis:** the patch is last-write-wins on a monotonic `progress` from a single runner (the engine owns the row end-to-end, B-7.1 finding), so out-of-order socket frames can at worst show a momentarily lower % that the next frame or the `done` refetch corrects — no corruption, no lost terminal state (done→invalidate is authoritative). `stage: e.stage ?? j.stage` preserves the last known stage if a frame omits it. **Leak:** `onRealtime` returns an unsubscribe fn (socket.ts:33); both `offProgress()`+`offDone()` run in the effect cleanup — symmetric, one subscription pair per shell mount (`useRealtimeJobs` mounted once in Layout, mirroring `useRealtimeNotifications`). No accumulation.
- **(3) DataGrid `invalidate(['jobs'])` string-key coupling — ACCEPTABLE (deliberate decoupling).** `DataGrid` is a generic `ui/` primitive; importing `features/jobs` (`JOBS_KEY`) into it would invert the dependency direction (ui → feature) and is the WORSE coupling — dependency-cruiser would likely flag it. The literal `['jobs']` keeps the primitive feature-free; it matches `JOBS_KEY = ['jobs']` (api.ts:5) by value. See FLAG-minor for the one hardening note.
- **(4) `NotificationBell` + `JobsTray` (components/) importing `features/jobs` — CONSISTENT with precedent.** `NotificationBell` ALREADY imports `features/notifications/useNotifications` (line 15); `Layout` already imports `features/notifications`. The new `features/jobs` imports (bell:16, JobsTray:12-13, Layout:10) follow the identical established components→features pattern. `pnpm boundaries` 0 errors confirms the rule permits it. `NotificationBell.downloadFromNotification` keys off `n.actionType==='DOWNLOAD'` (a real SDK enum member — `NOTIFICATION_ACTION_TYPES` includes `'DOWNLOAD'`, notifications.ts:23) and `n.payload?.['jobId']` guarded `typeof jobId !== 'string' → return` (safe under `noUncheckedIndexedAccess`; `payload` is `Record<string,unknown>`). No invented shape.
- **(5) 13-page `apiBlob→apiExport` swap — clean, no half-swap, no orphan import.** Diffed all 13 + MasterDataCrud: each `exportFn` body swapped `apiBlob(...)→apiExport(...)` (same URL, same `ExportRequest`), and each import line swapped `apiBlob→apiExport`. **UsersPage CORRECTLY keeps `apiBlob`** (import line: `api, apiBlob, apiExport, apiUpload, ApiError`) because its DataGrid `exportFn` uses `apiExport` (line 247) while a SEPARATE non-DataGrid scope export at line 209 (`apiBlob(`${BASE}/scope/export?mode=all&format=xlsx`)`) is a small always-synchronous file that must stay a direct download — so both helpers are genuinely used, no orphan. The other 12 pages dropped `apiBlob` from the import entirely (it was their only user). grep-spot-checked: no page left with a dangling `apiBlob` import nor a missed `exportFn`. `ExportResult` type import removed from DataGrid (replaced by `ExportOutcome`) — `ExportResult` still exported from the SDK for any other consumer; not orphaned at the SDK level.
- **(6) TS-strict / no-any / no-suppressions / `window.open` — PASS.** 0 suppressions (grep). The only casts are `JobsTray.jobResult` narrowing `j.result ?? {}` (a `Record<string,unknown>|null` JSONB field) to the read shape — an unavoidable deserialization narrowing, defensively `?? {}` + every field optional + `?? 0`/`?? 'file'` defaulted, so a malformed `result` degrades gracefully, never throws. `window.open(url, '_blank', 'noopener')` — `noopener` present on BOTH call sites (JobsTray:80, NotificationBell) → reverse-tabnabbing safe; the presigned URL is server-built (actor-namespaced `exports/${actorId}/...`), not user-controlled.

- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · `components/ui/data-grid/DataGrid.tsx` (job-branch `invalidate(['jobs'])`)** — the `['jobs']` literal duplicates `JOBS_KEY` by value with no compile-time link; if `JOBS_KEY` ever changes (e.g. to `['jobs', userId]`), this invalidate silently no-ops and a just-enqueued export won't appear in the tray until the next `job:progress`/`job:done` socket frame refetches it (so it self-heals within ~1s, hence minor not must-fix). Cheapest hardening that preserves the ui→feature decoupling: export the bare key string as an `@crm2/sdk` const (e.g. `JOBS_QUERY_KEY`) and reference it from both the feature and the grid — neither imports the other's module. Optional; the value-match is correct today and the socket refetch is a backstop.
- **INFO · `useJobs` has no `refetchInterval`** — the tray relies entirely on the socket for liveness (REST is the durable source, socket is the nudge — matching the notifications design). If the socket is down (degraded `noopRealtime`), an enqueued job sits at its last-fetched state until the next manual tray-driven refetch or page nav. Acceptable for the dev-only deployment and consistent with the notification feed's identical socket-dependence; a low-frequency `refetchInterval` while `activeCount>0` would be the belt-and-suspenders option if socket reliability becomes a concern. Not a defect.

**Bottom line:** the union + 202-detection is the strict safe reading of a BE-enforced contract; the realtime cache-patch is race-safe and leak-free; the 13-page swap is surgical with UsersPage's dual-helper retention correct; boundaries/typecheck/format/no-suppressions all independently green. The lone note (FLAG-minor #3) is a value-coupling hardening that self-heals via the socket. Cleared to commit.

### 2026-06-15 — B-7.2 Valkey + BullMQ out-of-process worker tier (ADR-0030; `platform/jobs/index.ts` getQueue/enqueue/startJobWorker/runJob, `main.ts` ROLE=worker boot, `http/registerJobs.ts` notifier moved out of `app.ts`, `platform/export/job.ts` + `packages/config` EXPORT_JOB_MAX_ROWS 200k, `docker-compose.yml` valkey:6380, ALLOWED_DEPENDENCIES +bullmq; working tree, uncommitted) — VERDICT: **PASS** (no BLOCK/must-fix; 2 FLAG-minor, 1 INFO)

Read every touched file + full `git diff`. Independently verified: `pnpm --filter @crm2/api typecheck` EXIT 0; old-vs-new `app.ts` (`git show HEAD:`) confirms the notifier wiring + its imports moved cleanly. The prior B-13 **F1 MUST-FIX is RESOLVED** here — `locations/service.ts exportAllForJob` now destructures `{ items, totalCount }` from `repo.list({…, limit: exportJobRowCap()})` and returns `totalCount`, so the processor's `capped = matched > rowCount` is correct; 157,074 < 200k cap ⇒ `capped:false` (the live verification is now honest, not a truncated file). The prior SHOULD-FIX (notifier `.notify` without `.catch`) is also RESOLVED — the wiring moved to `registerJobs.ts:16-20` WITH a `.catch(logger.warn)`.

- **(1) enqueue branch — CORRECT, no double-run.** `enqueue` (jobs/index.ts:154-172) is a strict `if (q) { q.add(...) } else { runJob in-process }` — mutually exclusive; when `REDIS_QUEUE_URL` is set it ONLY adds to the queue and never also runs in-process. The PENDING row is INSERTed first either way, so the tray row is identical. `inFlight` tracking is confined to the in-process branch (correct — tests await it; the queued path is awaited via the worker).
- **(2) getQueue tri-state cache — SOUND.** `undefined`=unresolved, `null`=disabled, `Queue`=live; `if (queue !== undefined) return queue` correctly returns a cached `null` (in-process) or the live Queue without re-reading env. See FLAG-minor #1 for the one race nuance.
- **(3) runJob exported + shared by both paths — no cross-process hazard.** `processors`/`notifier`/`queue`/`inFlight` are module-level but **per-process**; the worker independently calls `registerJobs()` (main.ts:32) BEFORE `startJobWorker()`, so its `processors` map + `notifier` are populated in-process. All durable state lives in Valkey (queue) and Postgres (job row) — no shared mutable JS state across the api↔worker boundary. Contract is identical (same `runJob`, same progress/notify/emit).
- **(4) notifier wiring app.ts→registerJobs — CLEAN, no orphan imports.** New `app.ts` imports only `jobRoutes` + `registerJobs` (no `setJobNotifier`/`notificationService`); `git show HEAD:app.ts` confirms those two imports + the wiring block were the only things removed and they now live solely in `registerJobs.ts`. `createApp` calls `registerJobs()` (app.ts:65); worker calls it (main.ts:32). No double-wire (each process boots once), no missing-wire, no orphan.
- **(5) EXPORT_JOB_MAX_ROWS via config — CLEAN.** `exportJobRowCap()=loadEnv().EXPORT_JOB_MAX_ROWS` (zod `coerce.number().int().positive().default(200000)`); the builder honors it as the `limit`, the processor surfaces `capped`+`logger.warn`. `bullmq` lazy-imported in BOTH getQueue + startJobWorker ⇒ the in-process/test path pulls nothing (grep confirms no top-level bullmq import). 0 `any`/suppressions in the slice; `import('bullmq').Queue|ConnectionOptions` type-only refs keep types without a runtime dep.

- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · `platform/jobs/index.ts:136-147` (`getQueue`)** — the lazy-cache check (`queue !== undefined`) and the assignment (`queue = new Queue(...)`) straddle an `await import('bullmq')`, so two concurrent first-`enqueue` calls (cold start, parallel requests) can both pass the guard and each construct a `Queue` — the second overwrites `queue`, orphaning the first ioredis connection (GC'd, but a transient duplicate socket). Harmless in practice (idempotent `add`, single dup at most), cheapest fix = cache the in-flight promise (`let queueP: Promise<Queue|null>`) instead of the resolved value. Optional.
- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · `platform/jobs/index.ts:125-134` (`connectionOpts`)** — parses `redis://` correctly (host, `port ?? 6379`, conditional user/pass, `maxRetriesPerRequest:null`), but a **`rediss://` (TLS) URL silently connects plaintext** — no `tls:{}` option is derived from the scheme. Dev/local Valkey is plaintext so this is latent, but a managed/TLS Valkey in prod would fail or downgrade. Fix when prod Valkey lands: `...(u.protocol === 'rediss:' ? { tls: {} } : {})`. Note, not gating (dev-only deploy today).
- **INFO · `q.add` sets `removeOnComplete:true, removeOnFail:500`, no `attempts`** — BullMQ defaults `attempts:1` (no auto-retry), which is the conservative correct choice for a non-idempotent-by-construction export (see RO ledger idempotency note); calling out so a future "add retries" change is made deliberately with the redelivery analysis in hand.

**Bottom line:** branch logic is correct (no double-run), the tri-state cache and per-process registration are sound, the notifier move is surgical with no orphans, and the B-13 F1/SHOULD-FIX it built on are both genuinely resolved. The two FLAG-minors (getQueue cold-start race, `rediss://` TLS) are latent and prod-facing, not dev-blocking. Cleared to commit.

### 2026-06-15 — B-14 background large-import tier (ADR-0030; `platform/import/index.ts` importMaxRows/assertImportable(max?)/runImportPreview+Confirm({maxRows})/ImportRunner registry/importJobProcessor/importConfirmOrEnqueue, `platform/import/format.ts` countImportRows, `platform/storage/index.ts` +get(), `packages/config` IMPORT_JOB_MAX_ROWS 200k, `modules/locations/{service,controller}`, `http/registerJobs.ts` IMPORT processor+locations runner, web `ImportModal.tsx`/`JobsTray.tsx`, `sdk/notifications.test.ts` + 4 storage fakes; working tree, uncommitted) — VERDICT: **PASS** (no BLOCK/must-fix; 2 FLAG-minor, 1 INFO)

Read every touched file + full `git diff`. Independently verified: `pnpm -w typecheck` EXIT 0 (8/8 FULL TURBO); `pnpm -w run boundaries` **0 errors** (14 pre-existing orphan warnings, all e2e/config, unrelated); grep across slice source = 0 `any`/`as any`/`@ts-ignore`/`@ts-expect-error`/`eslint-disable`/`console.*`. This is the import twin of the export tier I cleared on B-7/B-13/B-7.2; the engine seams match 1:1.

- **(1) `countImportRows` correctness — CORRECT for BOTH CSV + XLSX, and the prior 0-bug is genuinely fixed.** The earlier column-mapping approach returned 0 because `mapRows` needs the column manifest and `countImportRows` has none. The fix counts the **raw grid** instead: CSV → `parseCsvGrid(text).length - 1` (the SAME grid `parseImportCsv` builds; BOM stripped identically); XLSX → `ws.rowCount - 1` (the SAME `ws.rowCount` upper bound `parseImportXlsx`'s `for (r=2; r<=ws.rowCount; r++)` loop uses). Both subtract the header, both `Math.max(0, …)` floor an empty/header-only file to 0. **Semantics vs the actual processed count:** `countImportRows` is pre-blank-filter, `parseImportFile().length` is post-`mapRows`-`anyValue`-filter, so `count ≥ actual` — the routing decision can only *over*-route a near-boundary file to async, never *under*-route a real ≥10k file inline. Conservative, correct direction. The magic-byte sniff (`0x50 0x4b` = `PK`) is byte-identical to `parseImportFile`'s, so format detection can't diverge between the counter and the parser. Sound.
- **(2) `assertImportable(rowCount, max=importThreshold())` backward-compat — VERIFIED zero behavior change for the 9 un-wired modules.** Default param `max = importThreshold()` reproduces the old `rowCount >= threshold` throw exactly. `runImportPreview`/`runImportConfirm` thread `opts?.maxRows` → `assertImportable(rows.length, opts?.maxRows)`; when a module passes no `opts` (all 9 un-wired callers), `opts?.maxRows` is `undefined`, which re-triggers the default → still throws `IMPORT_TOO_LARGE` 413 at ≥10k. Only `locations` passes `{ maxRows: importMaxRows() }` (200k) on BOTH preview and confirm, lifting its inline-parse ceiling to the hard cap (because its real sync-vs-job gate now lives in `importConfirmOrEnqueue`, not in the parse throw). The error message/detail shape changed (`{rowCount, threshold}` → `{rowCount, max}`) but that's the same `IMPORT_TOO_LARGE` code/status — no contract break. grep-confirmed no non-locations caller passes `opts`. No behavior change.
- **(3) `importConfirmOrEnqueue` registry + worker re-run — SOUND, round-trip correct.** Decision: `count < threshold` → run the registered runner inline (`{kind:'result'}`); `count >= threshold` → `storage.put` the raw bytes at `imports/${userId}/${uuid}.bin` then `enqueue('IMPORT', {resource, storageKey, fileName, userId})` (`{kind:'job'}`). The closure is **NOT serialized** — the payload is 100% JSON (resource string + storageKey + fileName + userId), and the worker re-derives the runner from the per-process `importRunners` map populated by its own `registerJobs()` boot (same discipline I verified for export builders on B-7.2; the worker calls `registerJobs()` before `startJobWorker()`). The `importJobProcessor` round-trip is correct: `storage.get(storageKey)` → `runner(buffer, {userId, fileName})` → counts result → `storage.remove(storageKey)` best-effort cleanup with the comment correctly noting import_log is the durable record (so a cleanup failure can't lose the audit). **Ordering is correct and necessary:** `assertImportable(count, importMaxRows())` runs BEFORE the put/enqueue, so a >200k file is rejected without ever storing bytes. Note vs export: export keys by `ctx.jobId` (deterministic, post-enqueue, set inside the processor); import keys by `randomUUID()` because the file must be stored BEFORE enqueue (the storageKey is an enqueue input) — a forced ordering difference, not a defect; both are per-user-namespaced and unique.
- **(4) `storage.get` — COMPLETE across interface + all 3 providers + all 5 test fakes.** Added to `StorageProvider` interface; real S3 = `GetObjectCommand` → `out.Body.transformToByteArray()` → `Buffer.from(...)`, with `if (!out.Body) throw notConfigured()` (no 500 on an empty body); `disabledStorage.get` = `Promise.reject(notConfigured())` (clean 503, mirrors `put`); the 5 test fakes (cases, storage-mail, users×2, jobs) all stub it — jobs uses a real Map-backed `put`/`get`/`remove` so the IMPORT round-trip is genuinely exercised, the others return `Buffer.from('')` (they never read). grep `setStorage(` = exactly those 4 test files; users has 2 fakes = 5 total. The new `jobs.api.test.ts` case asserts the full path: small file → `kind:'result'`; 10k-row file → `kind:'job'` → `awaitAllJobs()` → `GET /jobs/:id` → `{type:'IMPORT', status:'SUCCEEDED', result:{totalRows,successRows,failedRows}}`. Complete.
- **(5) LAYERING — platform→platform, NO cycle, TS-strict.** `platform/import/index.ts` now imports `platform/jobs` (enqueue, JobProcessor) + `platform/storage` (getStorage) — both intra-platform, same direction `platform/export/job.ts` already imports them. grep-confirmed `platform/jobs/index.ts` does NOT import `platform/import` (it imports only `@crm2/sdk`, `@crm2/logger`, realtime, repository) → **no cycle** (import→jobs is one-directional). Module knowledge (`locationService`) enters only at the `http/registerJobs.ts` boot seam (the runner closure), exactly mirroring the export builder wiring — the import ENGINE stays module-free. `boundaries` 0 errors confirms. `DONE_TITLE`/`FAIL_TITLE` `Record<JobType,...>` both carry `IMPORT` keys (typecheck would fail otherwise), and the completion `actionType` is `NAVIGATE` for IMPORT (`type==='EXPORT' ? 'DOWNLOAD' : 'NAVIGATE'`) — correct, an import has no artifact to download. `NO_IMPORT_RUNNER` is a free-form code via `AppError.badRequest(code: ErrorCode|string)` — allowed. The only casts are `ctx.payload as {...}` (queue-deserialization narrowing of `unknown`, guarded by `if (!runner) throw`) and the `exceljs` Buffer type-skew bridge already present in format.ts — no new suppressions.
- **(6) FE 202 discrimination `'successRows' in res` — ROBUST.** `JobView` (sdk/jobs.ts) has NO top-level `successRows` (its counts are nested under `result: Record<string,unknown>`); `ImportConfirmResult` (sdk/import.ts:34) HAS top-level `successRows`. So `'successRows' in res` cleanly partitions the union `ImportConfirmResult | JobView` the FE typed the response as — the inline result has the key, the 202 JobView never does. Probed the inverse: the BE returns 202+JobView EXCLUSIVELY from the `out.kind==='job'` branch (no body that could carry `successRows`), and a synchronous result is always the `ImportConfirmResult`. The narrowing is the strict safe reading of a BE-enforced contract; on the job branch the FE invalidates `['jobs']`, toasts, and `reset()`s the modal — correct. (`JobsTray` reads the IMPORT result via the same optional-narrowed `jobResult()` with `?? 0` defaults — a malformed result degrades, never throws.)

- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · `platform/import/format.ts:165-178` (`countImportRows`) — the file is parsed TWICE on the inline path.** For a `<10k` import, `importConfirmOrEnqueue` calls `countImportRows(buffer)` (full `parseCsvGrid`/`exceljs.load`) for the routing decision, then the runner calls `runImportConfirm` which calls `parseImportFile(buffer)` — a SECOND full parse of the same bytes. For a 10k XLSX that's two `exceljs.load`s of the whole workbook. Harmless for the catalog sizes in play and it keeps the count/route concern cleanly separated from the spec-bound parse, but it's redundant CPU on every inline import. Cheapest fix if it ever matters: have the runner accept an already-parsed grid, or skip the count entirely below a cheap size heuristic. Optional — not gating.
- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · `platform/import/index.ts` (`importConfirmOrEnqueue` ≥threshold path) — storage-disabled failure surfaces only at confirm time.** If object storage is unconfigured (`disabledStorage`), a ≥10k confirm calls `getStorage().put(...)` which rejects with the 503 `notConfigured()` — so a large import on a storage-less deployment fails AT confirm (honest 503), but there's no earlier preflight telling the operator "background import needs storage" the way the runner-registry is checked up front (`if (!runner) throw NO_IMPORT_RUNNER`). Same latent shape as the export tier (which also assumes storage when enqueuing), and the live deploy has storage configured, so it's latent. Note for whoever wires the next storage-less environment; not gating.
- **INFO · the IMPORT job result intentionally drops `errors[]`** — the processor returns only the four counts; per-row failures live in `import_log` and the count surfaces as `failedRows` in the tray. Engineering-wise this is a clean subset of `ImportConfirmResult` through `JobView.result`, no invented shape; the follow-up (store `errors[]` alongside the file and expose a job artifact, mirroring the export download) is the symmetric enhancement. Flagged for the carry, not a defect.

**Bottom line:** `countImportRows` is correct for CSV+XLSX and conservative at the boundary; `assertImportable`'s default-param keeps the 9 un-wired modules byte-identical while locations opts into the 200k ceiling; the registry/worker re-run is closure-free and JSON-serializable with a correct store-before-enqueue ordering and a guarded round-trip; `storage.get` is complete across the interface, all 3 providers, and all 5 fakes (with a real Map-backed round-trip test); layering is platform-internal with no cycle; and the FE `'successRows' in res` is the strict safe reading of a BE-enforced 202 contract. typecheck 8/8 + boundaries 0 errors independently reconfirmed. The two FLAG-minors (double-parse on the inline path, storage-disabled-at-confirm) are latent/perf, not dev-blocking. Cleared to commit.

### 2026-06-15 — B-5 Saved DataGrid views (own-user; `db/v2/migrations/0051_saved_views.sql`, new module `modules/saved-views/{repository,service,controller,routes}.ts` + `__tests__/saved-views.api.test.ts`, web `components/ui/data-grid/SavedViewsPicker.tsx` + DataGrid.tsx mount, `sdk/savedViews.ts` + test, `sdk/{client,client.test,index}.ts`, `http/app.ts` mount; working tree, uncommitted) — VERDICT: **PASS** (no BLOCK/must-fix; 1 FLAG-minor, 1 INFO)

Read every new file + full `git diff` + the notifications/jobs siblings it mirrors. Independently verified: `pnpm --filter @crm2/api typecheck` EXIT 0; grep across the whole slice (api module + SDK leaf + FE picker + migration) = 0 `any`/`as any`/`@ts-ignore`/`@ts-expect-error`/`eslint-disable`/`console.*`. This is a faithful third instance of the own-user-scoped tray pattern (notifications 0045 / jobs 0050) — the seams match 1:1.

- **(1) LAYERING + boundaries — CLEAN.** controller→service→repository; controller does NOT import repository (grep-confirmed); raw SQL (`SELECT/INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE`) appears ONLY in repository.ts (grep on controller+service = empty). No permission gate by design (identity scope like /notifications, /jobs) — documented in the route header + service/migration comments.
- **(2) own-user scope / IDOR — ENFORCED at the repo, no cross-user path.** EVERY read and write carries `WHERE … user_id = $N` (listByResource, update, remove, setDefault's ownership probe + both UPDATEs). A non-owner `:id` yields 0 rows → repo returns `null`/`false` → service maps to 404 (not 403, IDOR-safe — can't distinguish "not yours" from "absent"). Controller `requireUserId` 401s pre-query; `requireUuid` shape-validates `:id` against `UUID_RE` → clean 404 (avoids pg 22P02→500), the same guard notifications/jobs use. Test proves all four: 401 unauth, 404 non-owner (PUT/DELETE/set-default), 404 unknown-uuid, 404 non-uuid.
- **(3) `withTransaction` in create + setDefault — CORRECT, partial-unique invariant holds.** `create(isDefault)`: clears any sibling default THEN inserts, in ONE tx → the partial unique index `uq_saved_views_default (user_id,resource_key) WHERE is_default` can never see two trues. `setDefault(true)`: ownership-probe → clear siblings `AND id <> $3` → set this row, all in one tx. `withTransaction` (platform/db.ts:34) does BEGIN/COMMIT, ROLLBACK-on-throw, and `client.release()` in `finally` — no leaked client. Test proves the at-most-one-default invariant across create-default, switch, and clear (filter `isDefault` always ≤1).
- **(4) error mapping (409/404/400/401) — CORRECT, with one over-broad catch noted.** 23505→`SAVED_VIEW_NAME_EXISTS` 409 (mirrors master-data code-exists); ZodError→400 via the central app.ts:106 handler (`CreateSavedViewSchema.parse`/`UpdateSavedViewSchema.parse`/`SetDefaultSavedViewSchema.parse` throw on bad shape); empty-update-body→400 via the `.refine(name||state)`; missing `resourceKey`→`RESOURCE_KEY_REQUIRED` 400. `AppError` 404s for absent rows. All exercised by the api test (409 dup same-grid; same name on another grid/user OK; 400 empty body; 400 no resourceKey). See FLAG-minor for the catch breadth.
- **(5) `state` jsonb round-trip — CORRECT, keys preserved verbatim.** `camelize` (db.ts:19) only transforms TOP-LEVEL row columns, so the jsonb `state` VALUE is returned untouched — its URL keys (`q`, `sort`, `f_<col>`, `f_<col>_from`…) must NOT be camelized, and they aren't. Write side `JSON.stringify(state)` + `$N::jsonb`. Test asserts `state` echoes byte-identically through create + update. `SavedViewStateSchema = z.record(z.string().max(64), z.string().max(2000))` bounds key/value size (row sanity); test rejects non-string values.
- **(6) FE auto-apply effect + `appliedDefault` ref — NO double-apply / stale-closure / infinite-loop.** `useEffect` deps `[viewsQuery.isLoading, viewsQuery.data, params, applyState]` include the UNMEMOIZED `applyState` AND `params` (both mutate on every apply), so the effect re-fires after it calls `setParams` — BUT `appliedDefault.current` is set `true` as the FIRST statement past the guard, so every re-fire early-returns. Single apply, no loop. The ref is set before the `hasState`/`def` checks, so even the "no default / has-state / error" branches still latch (apply happens at most once per mount); grid remounts per route so a default re-applies on nav-back, a bookmarked filtered URL is respected (`hasState` short-circuit). Race-free: `setParams(replace:true)` is idempotent under the latch. `captureState`→`applyState` URL round-trip drops `page` on capture (a view is a query, not a scroll position) — symmetric with the migration/SDK comments.
- **(7) SDK leaf + contract — CLEAN.** `savedViews.ts` is zod-only (no runtime dep); `client.ts` adds 5 typed methods (`list` URL-encodes `resourceKey`; create/update/remove/setDefault), re-exported via `index.ts` BEFORE `client.js`. `client.test.ts` bumps the transport call-count 128→133 (+5) and asserts the list URL — the count-invariant correctly tracks the new leaves. FE picker uses the web `api<T>()` directly (the established unchecked-cast helper; shape matches the SDK `SavedView`).

- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · `modules/saved-views/repository.ts:59-62, 91-94` — the 23505 catch is broader than the name constraint.** Both `create` and `update` map ANY unique violation to `SAVED_VIEW_NAME_EXISTS` (409), but the table has TWO unique constraints: `uq_saved_views_user_resource_name` (name) and the partial `uq_saved_views_default` (one-default). In normal operation the default-index can't fire (both default-setting paths clear siblings in the same tx before writing), so today every 23505 IS the name clash and the mapping is correct. But if a future change ever lets a second `is_default=true` slip through, it'd surface as a misleading "name already exists". Cheapest hardening: branch on `e.constraint === 'uq_saved_views_user_resource_name'` before mapping to NAME_EXISTS. Optional — currently unreachable.
- **INFO · FE `applyState` drops empty-string values (`if (v)` at SavedViewsPicker.tsx:43) while `captureState` copies them.** A view whose saved state held a `''` value would not re-apply that key. The DataGrid URL contract clears filters by removing the key (never empties it), so this asymmetry is unreachable in practice — flagged for awareness, not a defect.

**Bottom line:** faithful third instance of the own-user tray pattern — layering clean, scope enforced at the repo with IDOR-safe 404s, the two `withTransaction` paths hold the partial-unique one-default invariant atomically, error mapping (401/400/404/409) is correct and test-proven, the jsonb `state` round-trips with keys intact, and the FE auto-apply effect is single-shot/loop-free via the `appliedDefault` latch. typecheck EXIT 0, 0 suppressions/any/console, comprehensive api test (own-user isolation, all status codes, single-default). The one FLAG-minor (over-broad 23505 catch) is currently unreachable. Cleared to commit.

- **2026-06-15 — B-11/B-12 — OpenAPI surface + SDK-drift gate (ADR-0031), working tree (uncommitted). VERDICT: PASS.**
  Read ADR-0031 + every new file + full `git diff`. Independently ran `pnpm --filter @crm2/api typecheck` (EXIT 0) and the
  contract suite (`vitest run src/platform/openapi --coverage=false` → **3/3 PASS**, 28ms). Adversarial probes below.
  - **(1) ZERO new dependency — CONFIRMED.** `git diff` on root + `apps/api/package.json`: only `scripts` added
    (`openapi`), no `dependencies`/`devDependencies` line. The CLI runner `tsx` ALREADY existed (api `devDependencies` :43,
    `^4.16.0`). No `@asteasolutions/zod-to-openapi` (correctly deferred to phase 2). The ADR's zero-dep claim holds exactly.
  - **(2) LAYERING — CLEAN, infra-only, DB-FREE.** `platform/openapi/{document,cli}.ts` import only `express` types, `node:fs`,
    `node:url`, `../../http/app.js`, `@crm2/logger`. grep for `pool|repositor|withTransaction|new Pool|.query(|getPool` across the
    module = NONE (only a doc-comment in cli.ts mentions "never touches the pool"). `buildOpenApiDocument` is pure `app → doc`.
    `createApp()` reads only `process.env['NODE_ENV']` at construction (no DB connect) so `pnpm openapi` and the test run DB-free —
    proven: the suite ran with no pool and the CLI regen below produced byte-identical output with no DB up.
  - **(3) TS-strict / no `any` / no suppressions — CLEAN.** grep `any|<any>|as any|ts-ignore|ts-expect-error|eslint-disable|console.`
    across the module = NONE. The two `app as unknown as { _router?…; router?… }` casts (document.ts:57-58) are the SOUND escape
    hatch: `_router`/`router` are genuinely absent from `@types/express`, the target is a structurally-typed `RouterLike`/`RouteLayer`
    (not `any`), and the `_router ?? router` fallback pre-handles the Express-5 root rename. The test's `as unknown` on `JSON.parse`
    is idiomatic.
  - **(4) DRIFT GATE HAS REAL TEETH — PROVEN.** Injected a phantom `/api/v2/__phantom__` path into the committed `openapi.json` and
    re-ran the suite → `the committed openapi.json is up to date` test **FAILED** (deepEqual catches it); restored, tree clean. The
    `toEqual(buildOpenApiDocument(app))` genuinely compares committed-vs-live. CI step 7+8 (`pnpm openapi` then
    `git diff --exit-code -- openapi.json`) is the same gate at the file level; the contract test enforces it in `pnpm test` too.
    Removed the old dead `--if-present`/`sdk:gen` stub → unconditional `pnpm openapi` (script chain root→api→`tsx cli.ts` resolves).
  - **(5) DETERMINISM — CONFIRMED.** Re-ran `pnpm openapi`; regenerated `openapi.json` is **byte-identical** to the committed file
    (no dirty tree). Determinism comes from `JSON.stringify(doc,null,2)+'\n'` over a route list `.sort((a,b)=> path||method)` — total
    order, stable git-diff. `.prettierignore` correctly excludes the file (format gate would otherwise reformat the deterministic JSON
    and fight the generator). Trailing newline present. 180 path templates / 201 operations; no duplicate operationIds (`uniq -d` empty).
  - **(6) ROUTE-WALK CORRECTNESS.** Recursion handles nested routers (`layer.name==='router' && layer.handle?.stack` → recurse with
    `mountPrefix(layer.regexp)`); leaf routes prefix-joined, trailing-slash normalized (`replace(/\/+$/,'') || '/'`), filtered to
    `/api/v2`. The empty-walk guard (`listApiRoutes(app).length > 100`) catches a silently-broken walk. Security cleared only for the
    4 `PUBLIC_PATHS` (health/time/auth.login/auth.refresh) — matches the pre-auth mounts.
  - **(7) SDK→route parity matcher — ROBUST, no false-negative.** `normSdk` runs the `${…}→:p` replacement FIRST, so multi-segment
    templated paths survive (verified: `/clients/${id}/activate → /clients/:p/activate`); the `[$?\`'"\s].*$` cut only trims a
    genuinely-dangling `${`/query-string tail. `reqBlob('<res>')→/api/v2/<res>/export` handled. All SDK paths are literal
    `/api/v2/...` strings (no dynamic base concatenation that would evade the regex). Reverse (route→SDK) intentionally NOT asserted —
    correct per ADR (the `api()`-called import/bulk/export/dashboard routes would rot an allowlist; git-diff covers them).
  - **FLAG-minor (non-gating, future-facing) · `document.ts:48-52` `mountPrefix` regexp parser is Express-4-specific.** It parses the
    `^\/…\/?(?=\/|$)` shape that Express-4's path-to-regexp v0 emits. On a future **Express-5 upgrade** (path-to-regexp v8 emits a
    different regexp), this parser returns a garbage prefix (simulated: `/api/v2/clients(?:/(?=$))?…`). MITIGATED — the failure is
    **LOUD, not silent**: garbage prefixes drop routes out of the `/api/v2` filter → `listApiRoutes` length collapses below the
    `>100` guard AND the committed-spec deepEqual fails, so CI/the test block the upgrade rather than emitting a wrong spec. The
    `_router ?? router` root fallback already anticipates v5; the prefix parser does not. When v5 is taken on, re-derive `mountPrefix`
    (or prefer the v5 `layer.matchers`/`path` if exposed). Acceptable for phase 1 on Express 4.22.2 (in use). Flagged for awareness.
  - **INFO · phase-1 scope (per ADR, accepted):** operations carry no request/response schema bodies (only paths/methods/tags/
    security). Response-shape drift is NOT caught until phase 2 (responses→zod). Request drift already structurally prevented by the
    shared `Create*Schema` zod. The `info.description` + `responses.default` text say so — omitted, not forgotten. Registry B-11/B-12
    rows + the CI comment accurately scope this as "validate-don't-replace, phase 1".
  - **Scope discipline (Karpathy):** surgical — 3 new module files + 1 artifact + 1 ADR + 4 narrowly-edited config files (ci/2×
    package.json/prettierignore) + registry. No adjacent refactor; the only deletion is the dead `--if-present` CI stub it replaces.

  **Bottom line:** the gate is real (drift injection fails the deepEqual; CI git-diffs the artifact), deterministic (byte-stable
  regen), zero-new-dep (tsx pre-existed), pure infra (DB-free `app→doc`, no repository/DB reach), TS-strict (no `any`/suppressions;
  the `unknown→RouterLike` casts are sound), and the SDK-parity direction is the correct high-signal one. typecheck EXIT 0, contract
  suite 3/3, `pnpm verify` reported EXIT 0. The one FLAG-minor (Express-4-coupled `mountPrefix`) fails LOUDLY on a future v5 bump, not
  silently — a phase-1-acceptable maintenance note, not a defect. **Cleared to commit.**

- **2026-06-15 — Lifecycle redesign (ADR-0032, DESIGN-ONLY review of `docs/specs/2026-06-15-lifecycle-design/2026-06-15-v2-lifecycle-redesign.md`). VERDICT: FLAG (approve-with-changes; no BLOCK).**
  Adversarial design review of the two-track Case/Task state machines + rollup service + the ADR-0025 per-task-result demotion. Verified §2/§3/§4/§6 against live v2 code (cases `repository.ts`/`service.ts`, sync `service.ts`, FE `CaseDetailPage.tsx`, mig 0037/0041).
  - **State machines — reachability/correctness (mostly sound):**
    - TASK track: all 6 authoritative states reachable; the §5 ingest finally gives `IN_PROGRESS` a producer (start) and `COMPLETED` a field producer (complete) — closes audit §6.2 (4-of-7 dead states). `SUBMITTED_FOR_REVIEW` correctly drops to non-authoritative; device normalizes SFR→COMPLETED so removal is **device-safe** (confirmed sync/service.ts:41 maps only REVOKED; SFR never emitted downward). CONFIRMED safe.
    - **MUST-FIX (M1) — CASE machine has an unreachable terminal + a missing edge.** §3 table lists `any → REVOKED` (case revoke) but the **rollup ladder in §3 prose omits REVOKED entirely** (`REVOKED-all → COMPLETED(office) → AWAITING_COMPLETION → IN_PROGRESS → NEW`). "REVOKED-all" (all tasks revoked) is a DIFFERENT trigger than the explicit `case.revoke` whole-case action — the design conflates two REVOKED paths. Pin down: is case-REVOKED a manual office action ONLY, or also auto when every task is REVOKED? If auto, the ladder needs an explicit "all-tasks-REVOKED ⇒ case REVOKED" rung ABOVE COMPLETED; if manual-only, drop "REVOKED-all" from the rollup prose. As written the two contradict.
    - **MUST-FIX (M2) — `AWAITING_COMPLETION → IN_PROGRESS` (revisit/new-task) bypasses the COMPLETED terminal trap.** Good (matches v1), but the ladder says COMPLETED is "NEVER auto" and only `case.finalize` sets it — yet there is **no rung preventing rollup from moving a COMPLETED case back to AWAITING_COMPLETION/IN_PROGRESS** when a revisit task is added post-finalize. §7 says revisit → case IN_PROGRESS. So COMPLETED is NOT terminal under revisit. Either (a) declare COMPLETED non-terminal (re-openable by revisit) and document the rollup rung `COMPLETED + new active task ⇒ IN_PROGRESS`, or (b) forbid revisit on a COMPLETED case. The design states both implicitly. Resolve.
  - **Rollup service design (FLAG):**
    - "in-tx after every task status write" + "COMPLETED never auto" is **correct** — rollup ceiling = AWAITING_COMPLETION, only `case.finalize` crosses to COMPLETED. Good separation.
    - **SHOULD-FIX (S1) — N+1 / deadlock ordering unspecified.** `recompute(caseId)` runs inside the SAME tx as the task write. It must (a) take a row lock on `cases` AFTER the `case_tasks` write to avoid the classic child→parent vs parent→child deadlock under concurrent task writes on one case, and (b) be a SINGLE aggregate query (`SELECT count(*) FILTER (WHERE status…)`), NOT a per-task loop. Bulk-assign funnels N task writes through `assignTask` (tasks/service.ts) — if rollup fires per-row inside the batch that's N rollup recomputes in one request. Design must state: rollup is ONE recompute at end-of-batch, or idempotent-and-cheap per write. Cite the lock-ordering rule explicitly (lock `cases` last, consistent order) or it WILL deadlock under the bulk-assign path.
    - **SHOULD-FIX (S2) — the existing `addTasks` NEW→IN_PROGRESS flip (repository.ts:380) is plain `WHERE status='NEW'`, NOT OCC-versioned** (audit §6.8). The redesign introduces a real rollup but doesn't say it REPLACES this ad-hoc flip. It must, or you'll have two case-status writers with different concurrency models. Fold the NEW→IN_PROGRESS into `recompute`.
  - **ADR-0025 demotion — clean? (FLAG):**
    - Demotion of `case_tasks.verification_outcome` → case-level `cases.verification_outcome` is architecturally coherent and fixes v1's VT-000199 fragmentation. BUT the demotion is **NOT clean against live readers.** Grepped: `case_tasks.verification_outcome` is read by (1) **FE `CaseDetailPage.tsx:243-246`** (renders per-task outcome badge via `KYC_RESULT_LABELS`), (2) **sync `service.ts` / `sync.ts:45`** `verificationOutcome?` device field, (3) **SDK `cases.ts:147`** `verificationOutcome: KycResult|null` on the task view, (4) the **complete writer + audit + notification body** (`service.ts:314`, `repository.ts:650/668`), (5) **test `cases.api.test.ts:748,755`** asserts `tasks[0].verificationOutcome==='POSITIVE'`.
    - **MUST-FIX (M3):** §4/§6 say the per-task column is "demoted to optional note OR dropped" and "never printed" — but the design does NOT enumerate these 5 readers or specify the migration path for each. If you keep the column note-only, the FE badge + SDK type + test still read it (fine, but they now show a NON-authoritative value next to the authoritative case result → exactly the dual-display confusion that caused VT-000199). If you drop it, all 5 break. This is the **API/Contract array→envelope-class trap** for this slice: a response-shape change with un-enumerated consumers. The design MUST list every reader and its disposition before slice 1. (Hand this to API/Contract auditor too.)
    - The **field `complete` path currently REQUIRES a result** (`CompleteTaskSchema { result: enum, remark: min1 }`, cases.ts:334). Under D1 (field submits evidence ONLY, no result), the §5 `/complete` ingest endpoint must use a DIFFERENT schema (no `result`) than the web desk-complete — but §5 reuses one `/complete`. **MUST-FIX (M4):** the field auto-complete and the desk-complete (which still sets per-task note?) cannot share `CompleteTaskSchema` as-is; field complete writes NO outcome. Split the schema or the field ingest will 400 on the required `result`.
  - **Layering / OCC / reuse (PASS):** §5 endpoints stay controller→service→repo; OCC `version` bump on every writer is explicitly carried (closes the TOCTOU note from prior ledger entries). Reuse of TaskCompletion path / `case_attachments` / ADR-0021 storage seam is correct (reuse-over-reinvent). New perms (`task.execute`/`task.revoke`/`case.finalize`/`case.revoke`) are additive default-deny — sound, but **NOTE:** the result enum is still named `KYC_RESULTS`/`KycResult` while now case-level+generic (audit §6.4 misnaming) — rename to `VERIFICATION_RESULT` in the same slice that touches the column or the misnomer ossifies.
  - **§10 slice ordering (FLAG):** Slice 1 (rollup + finalize + case result) before Slice 2 (ingest) is **backwards for verification** — you can't E2E the rollup-to-AWAITING_COMPLETION transition until tasks can actually reach COMPLETED via the field path (Slice 2). Slice 1 alone can only test desk-complete. Acceptable IF Slice 1 tests use desk-complete to drive tasks terminal; flag that the AWAITING_COMPLETION rollup is only fully exercised after Slice 2. Also **Slice 6 (mobile rebase) last** means the device stays on v1 `/api/mobile` through Slices 1-5 — so the §5 `/api/v2` ingest has NO real consumer until Slice 6; ensure Slice 2 ships contract-tests against the locked shapes (not a live device) or it's untestable until the end.
  - **Net:** the two-track model is the right call and most invariants hold. FLAG (not BLOCK) — M1-M4 are design-completeness gaps (unreachable/contradictory edges, un-enumerated demotion readers, shared-schema collision) that must be pinned in the doc before slice 1 builds, not architectural dead-ends. No BLOCK. OPEN carried: enumerate the 5 `case_tasks.verification_outcome` readers + disposition; lock-ordering spec for rollup; field-vs-desk complete schema split; KYC_RESULTS rename.

### 2026-06-15 — slice-1 commit review (ADR-0032 case lifecycle spine; `db/v2/migrations/0052_case_lifecycle.sql` + `modules/cases/{repository,service,controller,routes}.ts` + `packages/access/permissions.ts` + `sdk/{cases,client}.ts` + web `CaseDetailPage.tsx` + `openapi.json` + `cases.api.test.ts`; working tree, uncommitted). VERDICT: **PASS** (no BLOCK/must-fix; 1 FLAG-minor, 2 INFO). All my prior M1/M2/S1/S2 design gaps are resolved IN CODE.
- **Independently verified:** `pnpm --filter @crm2/api typecheck` + `@crm2/sdk typecheck` BOTH EXIT 0; grep `any|as any|ts-ignore|ts-expect-error|eslint-disable|console.` across all 6 slice source files = 0 (4 hits, all in comments). The `cases.api` suite is `RUN`-gated and self-skips here (test DB :5433/:54329 down in sandbox — `pg_isready` no-response on both), so I could not EXECUTE the 3 new finalize/rollup tests; I read them line-by-line (below) and they are correct. Flag to whoever runs gate: confirm the suite GREEN against a live test DB before commit.
- **(1) `recomputeCaseStatus` IS the single case-status writer — CONFIRMED.** The old inline `addTasks` flip (`UPDATE cases SET status='IN_PROGRESS' … WHERE status='NEW'`, ex-repository.ts:380) is fully DELETED and replaced by `recomputeCaseStatus(q,caseId,userId)` (resolves my S2). grep: every `cases` status mutation outside finalize now routes through recompute — called in `addTasks` (post-INSERT), `assignTask` (post-history), `unassignTask` (post-history), `completeTask` (post-result-write). No residual ad-hoc `UPDATE cases SET status` anywhere. Two writers total by design: `recomputeCaseStatus` (auto, ceiling = AWAITING_COMPLETION) and `finalizeCase` (manual, the ONLY COMPLETED setter) — clean separation.
- **(2) lock-first race fix + lock ordering — CORRECT (comment is self-contradictory in WORDING only).** recompute does `SELECT status FROM cases WHERE id=$1 FOR UPDATE` as its FIRST stmt, THEN the single aggregate `count(*) FILTER(...)` over `case_tasks`, THEN the guarded UPDATE — so concurrent task-writers serialize on the cases row and each recompute reads the latest committed task states (kills the "both see one-active → stuck IN_PROGRESS" race; resolves my S1). GLOBAL lock order is `case_tasks → cases` in ALL 4 callers (the task UPDATE/INSERT acquires the task-row lock BEFORE recompute's `FOR UPDATE` on cases): verified in addTasks (INSERT→recompute), assignTask (UPDATE→history→recompute), completeTask (UPDATE→audit→recompute), unassignTask. No path locks cases before case_tasks → no deadlock. The doc-comment line "Locks the cases row FIRST" reads as contradicting "lock order is always tasks → cases" — both are TRUE under different scopes ("first thing recompute does" vs "global order"), but the wording is a footgun for the next reader → see FLAG-minor.
- **(3) rollup ladder — matches §3, NEVER COMPLETED, SKIPS REVOKED, verdict-clears on re-open.** `if (!cur || cur.status==='REVOKED') return` (manual-terminal + missing untouched — resolves M1: no auto-revoke). Ladder: 0 tasks→NEW · active>0→IN_PROGRESS · completed>0→AWAITING_COMPLETION · else→IN_PROGRESS (degenerate all-REVOKED/CANCELLED; office handles). COMPLETED is NOT a computed output (only finalize sets it) AND COMPLETED is re-openable: the guarded UPDATE `WHERE … status<>'REVOKED' AND status<>$2` always NULLs `verification_outcome/result_remark/completed_at/completed_by` on ANY status move, so a revisit/recheck adding an active task to a COMPLETED case → recompute moves it COMPLETED→IN_PROGRESS AND wipes the stale verdict (resolves M2 + §4 anti-staleness; test FIN3 proves verdict→null on re-open). version++ on the recompute UPDATE (writer bumps version — invariant held). The `status<>$2` guard makes recompute a no-op (0 rows, no version churn) when the computed status equals current — correct, idempotent.
- **(4) `finalizeCase` OCC + transition guard + 0-row disambiguation — CORRECT.** Service: `CaseFinalizeSchema.parse` → `requireVersion(input)` (client OCC token, 400 if absent) → `resolveScope` → `caseFinalizeState(caseId, scope)` (scope-guarded SELECT; null→404 IDOR-safe, resolves the Security case-grain-scope blocker) → transition pre-check `status!=='AWAITING_COMPLETION'→409 INVALID_TRANSITION` → repo. Repo: guarded `UPDATE … WHERE id=$1 AND version=$5 AND status='AWAITING_COMPLETION' RETURNING id`; 0 rows → re-SELECT → not found→404 / status≠AWAITING→409 INVALID_TRANSITION / else→`AppError.stale(cur)` 409. This is the canonical OCC 0-row disambiguation from my standing pattern, applied at CASE grain. version++ + audit row in the SAME tx. OCC token is the CLIENT version (not the pre-check read) — correct; a concurrent rollup bumping version between pre-check and UPDATE → guarded UPDATE 0-rows → stale 409 (no lost finalize). The double-status-guard (service pre-check AND repo WHERE) is intentional belt-and-suspenders, not redundant — the repo guard is the atomic one.
- **(5) layering / reuse — CLEAN.** Raw SQL only in repository (recompute, caseFinalizeState, finalizeCase all repo); service orchestrates (scope/transition/parse) + calls repo; controller is the std `res.json(await svc…); catch→next(e)`. Reuses `withTransaction`/`appendAudit`/`caseScopePredicate`/`requireVersion`/`AppError.stale`/`resolveScope` — zero reinvention. `TxQuery` type imported for the in-tx recompute signature (correct — recompute MUST run in the caller's tx, never opens its own). New perm `case.finalize` additive default-deny (BACKEND_USER + SA via grants_all), migration seeds `role_permissions` to match `ROLE_PERMISSIONS` (parity invariant), `PERMISSION_META` label added.
- **(6) migration 0052 — idempotent superset, no data migration.** `version int NOT NULL DEFAULT 1` (resolves DB M1), status CHECK drop-then-add is a strict superset (+AWAITING_COMPLETION/REVOKED → no backfill), verdict cols all `ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS`, `case_tasks.verification_outcome` (0041) KEPT not demoted (resolves my M3 — per-task result preserved; test FIN1 proves per-task POSITIVE coexists with case-verdict NEGATIVE). `started_at`/`form_data` added now for slice-2 read-model stability. role_permissions ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING. Forward-only.
- **(7) contract/enum widen — no broken reader (the array→envelope-class trap, enum variant).** `CASE_STATUSES` widened to 6; `CaseStatus`/`CASE_STATUS_LABELS` exported; `CaseView` gains `verificationOutcome/resultRemark/completedAt/version/completedByName`; `findById` + list both use `CASE_VIEW_SELECT` which now selects all 5 (camelize maps them). Sole consumers of the enum (`CasesPage` STATUS_OPTIONS, service sortMap + status-filter whitelist) auto-derive from `CASE_STATUSES` → new statuses appear as valid filters/sort automatically, no hardcoded reader breaks. `openapi.json` regenerated with the `/finalize` POST (drift gate satisfied; phase-1 no response schema, per ADR-0031). FE finalize form: exactOptionalProps-safe conditional spread for `remark`, gated `case.finalize`, STALE→reload hint, verdict shown only at COMPLETED.
- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · `repository.ts:80-82` recompute doc-comment self-contradiction.** "Locks the cases row FIRST (SELECT … FOR UPDATE)" vs "lock order is always tasks → cases" read as contradictory out of context. Both true (intra-recompute order vs global cross-table order), but a future maintainer touching a caller could "fix" the apparent contradiction and invert a lock. Cheapest fix: reword to "recompute's first stmt is the cases `FOR UPDATE`; callers always write `case_tasks` BEFORE calling recompute, so the global order is case_tasks→cases." Optional — code is correct as-is.
- **INFO · slice-1 desk-`/complete` still writes a per-task result (`CompleteTaskSchema` requires `result`).** This is the EXISTING desk path, untouched; the field-ingest no-result split is slice 2 (resolves M4 prospectively, not in this diff). Correct scope — flagged so the slice-2 reviewer confirms the field `/complete` uses a result-free schema.
- **INFO · degenerate all-REVOKED/CANCELLED case → IN_PROGRESS** (recompute final else-branch). A case whose every task is REVOKED/CANCELLED reads IN_PROGRESS, not a terminal — matches §3 prose ("office handles"); acceptable since case-REVOKED is manual-only. No active producer keeps it stuck (no rollup loop). Flagged for the Pipeline-bucket slice (4) so it surfaces in a sensible queue.
**Bottom line:** every design gap I raised (M1 two-REVOKED, M2 COMPLETED-not-terminal, S1 deadlock/race, S2 single-writer) is resolved IN CODE; the demotion trap (M3) is mooted by keeping the per-task column; recompute is the genuine single auto-writer with a correct lock-first race fix and consistent case_tasks→cases ordering; finalize is canonical CASE-grain OCC with proper 0-row disambiguation and case-scope (closes the Security blocker). typecheck 2/2 EXIT 0, 0 suppressions/any/console, openapi drift-clean, 3 new tests read correct. The lone FLAG-minor is a misleading comment, not a bug. **Cleared to commit — but RUN the `cases.api` suite against a live test DB first (couldn't execute in sandbox; both test DBs down).**

### 2026-06-15 — slice-2a/2b commit review (ADR-0032 Pipeline-SLA + dashboard; `modules/tasks/{repository,service}.ts`, `modules/dashboard/repository.ts`, `sdk/{tasks,dashboard}.ts`, web `pipeline/PipelinePage.tsx` + `dashboard/{DashboardPage,components/CounterBar}.tsx`, + 2 api tests). VERDICT: **PASS** (no BLOCK/must-fix; 2 FLAG-minor, 2 INFO).
- **Independently verified:** `@crm2/api` + `@crm2/sdk` + `@crm2/web` typecheck ALL EXIT 0; grep `awaitingReview` across apps/packages = 0 (stale-reader trap clean); `TaskStats.cancelled`/`'cancelled'` literal in tasks module = 0. Couldn't EXECUTE the two RUN-gated api suites (test DBs down in sandbox) — read both new tests line-by-line (correct). Flag to gate-runner: run `tasks.api` + `dashboard.api` green on a live test DB before commit.
- **(a) `SLA_BREACH_SQL` predicate — CORRECT + genuinely param-free.** OPEN-only (`ct.status IN ('PENDING','ASSIGNED','IN_PROGRESS')`) ANDed with `now() > ct.created_at + CASE ct.priority …`. `case_tasks.priority` is `varchar(10) NOT NULL DEFAULT 'MEDIUM'` + CHECK `IN ('LOW','MEDIUM','HIGH','URGENT')` (mig 0037) → the 4 WHEN arms cover the whole domain; `ELSE 48h` is unreachable-in-prod but a sensible default (NOT NULL ⇒ no NULL arm needed). No `$n` placeholders, references only `ct` → genuinely safe to inline THREE ways: (1) `TASK_SELECT` derived column `… AS out_of_tat`, (2) `buildWhere` list filter (`if (o.outOfTat) where.push(SLA_BREACH_SQL)` — placed AFTER ids/BEFORE columnFilters+scope, no param-index interaction since it pushes none), (3) `stats` FILTER aggregate. Terminal tasks (COMPLETED/REVOKED/SFR/CANCELLED) can never breach (status gate) — test proves complete→outOfTat 0. ✅
- **(b) stats refactor GROUP-BY-rows → conditional-FILTER — `total` now CORRECT (old was buggy).** Old: `total = pending+assigned+inProgress+completed+cancelled` (sum of 5 buckets) — which UNDER-counted (excluded REVOKED + SUBMITTED_FOR_REVIEW + the never-emitted CANCELLED). New `total = count(*)::int` = ALL rows in scope. This is a genuine FIX, not a regression. The Map-merge in the service (`new Map(rows…)` + manual sum) is fully deleted; repo now returns the typed `TaskStats` row directly with a `?? {…all-zero}` fallback (noUncheckedIndexedAccess-safe). **camelize bridge — all maps verified:** `in_progress→inProgress`, `out_of_tat→outOfTat` (toCamel `_([a-z])→upper`, db.ts:16) — both round-trip correctly; SELECT aliases match the SDK keys exactly. NOTE (INFO): CANCELLED + SUBMITTED_FOR_REVIEW rows are in `total` but in NO displayed chip → `sum(chips) ≤ total` by design (the bar isn't a partition; "All" is the superset). Acceptable.
- **(c) dashboard SLA DUPLICATED (`SLA_BREACH`) not imported — RIGHT call.** The dashboard repo ALREADY locally duplicates `caseScopePredicate` (+ `OPEN_HELD`) with an explicit "kept local to respect module boundaries" rationale, because cross-feature internal imports are dependency-cruiser-forbidden (standing invariant). Importing tasks' `SLA_BREACH_SQL` into dashboard would BE the boundary violation. The local copy is the established pattern in THIS file; the two copies are byte-equivalent semantics (formatting differs only). The DRY cost is a 7-line SQL constant — acceptable per the module-boundary invariant. See FLAG-minor #1 (drift risk). The `awaitingCompletion` 2nd query + `...(row ?? ZERO), awaitingCompletion: caseRow?.awaitingCompletion ?? 0` merge with `query<Omit<DashboardStats,'awaitingCompletion'>>` typing is CLEAN: the FILTER scan produces every DashboardStats key EXCEPT awaitingCompletion (correctly Omit-typed since that col isn't in the SELECT), the case query supplies it, the spread reconstructs the full type. `ZERO` fallback still carries `awaitingCompletion:0` (overwritten by the merge — harmless dead value). ✅
- **(d) N+1 / perf — dashboard now 2 queries (was 1) — ACCEPTABLE, not N+1.** It is 2 CONSTANT queries per request (one TASK-grain FILTER scan + one `count(*)` over `cases WHERE status='AWAITING_COMPLETION'`), NOT a per-row loop — no N+1. The 2nd is forced by GRAIN: `awaitingCompletion` is CASE-grain (cases table), the rest TASK-grain (`case_tasks ct JOIN cases cs`); they can't share one scan without double-counting cases with N tasks. Correct architectural split. The case query uses `caseScopePredicate(caseParams, scope)` with its OWN fresh `caseParams:[]` array (so `$1…` are independent of the task query's params) — verified `composeScopePredicate` pushes to the passed array and numbers `$${params.length}` off it → no cross-query param bleed. INFO: a future single-roundtrip optimization (CTE/`UNION ALL` of the two scalar shapes) is possible but premature; 2 scoped scans are cheap (no MV). Flagged, not gating.
- **(e) layering — CLEAN.** Raw SQL stays in both repositories; service does param-coercion + scope + buildPage only (`outOfTat = raw==='1'||raw==='true'`, conditional-spread into repo opts AND echoed `filters` — exactOptionalProps-safe); controllers untouched. No `any`/suppressions/`console.*` in the slice. FE: `selectBucket` makes status-vs-SLA buckets mutually exclusive (clears both keys, sets one), the ⚠TAT badge reads the derived `t.outOfTat`, `revoked` chip replaces `cancelled`, dashboard "Out of TAT" KPI + "Awaiting Completion" CounterBar cell route to `/pipeline?outOfTat=1` and `/cases?status=AWAITING_COMPLETION` respectively (the `to?` override is a clean additive optional). All consumers of the renamed SDK fields migrated in-slice (grep-proven).
- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · dashboard `SLA_BREACH` vs tasks `SLA_BREACH_SQL` will DRIFT silently.** Two hand-maintained copies of the same TAT ladder (12/24/48/72h). A future SLA-threshold change touching one and not the other yields dashboard-KPI ≠ Pipeline-bucket for the SAME tasks — a silent numeric inconsistency, not a crash. Module boundaries forbid the import, so the right fix when SLA becomes configurable (the code comment already anticipates "pending an SLA-config feature") is a SHARED source (config row / `@crm2/sdk` const both repos read), not a cross-module import. Acceptable today (constants identical); pin when SLA config lands.
- **FLAG-minor (non-gating) · dashboard `caseScopePredicate` `EXISTS (… ct.assigned_to = ANY($ph))` could double-count is N/A but the case-queue scope differs subtly from the task-queue scope.** The `awaitingCompletion` count is "cases visible by the CASE leg" (creator OR holds-an-in-scope-task) while the rest of the dashboard is "tasks visible by the TASK leg". For a case whose tasks are assigned outside the actor's scope but which the actor created, it counts in `awaitingCompletion` but its tasks don't appear in the task buckets — internally consistent per-grain but the two numbers answer different visibility questions. Matches the cases-module leg exactly (intended), flagged only so a reader doesn't expect chip-arithmetic across the two grains.
